## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: chemical reaction kinetics
**Analysis**: This task involves finding the rate of change of concentration (dA/dt) as a function of time and concentration A, which is a classic chemical kinetics problem. The rate law typically depends on concentration raised to some power (reaction order), and may involve complex mechanisms leading to various functional forms.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- {'name': 'Zero-order kinetics', 'formula': 'dA_dt = c0', 'scenario': 'Reaction rate independent of concentration'}
- {'name': 'First-order kinetics', 'formula': 'dA_dt = c0 * A', 'scenario': 'Rate proportional to concentration (radioactive decay, unimolecular decomposition)'}
- {'name': 'Second-order kinetics', 'formula': 'dA_dt = c0 * A**2', 'scenario': 'Rate proportional to square of concentration (bimolecular reaction)'}
- {'name': 'General n-th order kinetics', 'formula': 'dA_dt = c0 * A**c1', 'scenario': 'Generalized power-law rate with fractional or arbitrary reaction order'}
- {'name': 'Mixed-order kinetics', 'formula': 'dA_dt = c0 * A + c1 * A**2', 'scenario': 'Parallel first and second order reaction pathways'}
- {'name': 'Reversible first-order reaction', 'formula': 'dA_dt = c0 * A + c1', 'scenario': 'First-order forward reaction with reverse reaction approaching equilibrium'}
- {'name': 'Saturation kinetics (Lindemann-type)', 'formula': 'dA_dt = c0 * A / (c1 + A)', 'scenario': 'Unimolecular reaction with pressure-dependent falloff behavior'}
- {'name': 'Inhibition kinetics', 'formula': 'dA_dt = c0 * A / (c1 + A**2)', 'scenario': 'Substrate inhibition or self-inhibition at high concentration'}
- {'name': 'Autocatalytic kinetics', 'formula': 'dA_dt = c0 * A * (c1 - A)', 'scenario': 'Autocatalytic reaction where product catalyzes its own formation'}
- {'name': 'Time-dependent rate (photochemical)', 'formula': 'dA_dt = c0 * A * exp(c1 * t)', 'scenario': 'Rate with time-dependent external driving (e.g., light intensity change)'}
- {'name': 'Polynomial rate with equilibrium', 'formula': 'dA_dt = c0 * (A - c1) * (A - c2)', 'scenario': 'Reaction with two equilibrium concentrations or bistability'}
- {'name': 'Third-order kinetics', 'formula': 'dA_dt = c0 * A**3', 'scenario': 'Termolecular reaction or effective third-order process'}
- {'name': 'Combined power law with offset', 'formula': 'dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 + c2', 'scenario': 'Power-law kinetics with constant source or sink term'}

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Negative rate of change (consumption) → dA_dt typically has negative coefficient times positive powers of A
- Equilibrium approach → Rate expression contains (A - A_eq) factor indicating relaxation toward equilibrium concentration
- Autocatalysis → Product of A and (constant - A), creating logistic-like dynamics with a maximum rate at intermediate concentration
- Competing parallel pathways → Sum of power-law terms with different exponents: c0*A^n1 + c1*A^n2
- Concentration-dependent mechanism switch → Rational functions of A, reflecting dominant mechanism changing at different concentration regimes
- Conservation constraint → If total concentration is conserved, rate depends on A*(c-A) type terms from stoichiometric coupling
- Induction period or delay → Explicit time dependence in rate (e.g., multiplication by t or sigmoidal function of t) suggests initiation step
- Half-integer reaction orders → A**0.5 or A**1.5 terms suggest chain reaction mechanisms with radical intermediates
